## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:43:18]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Next.js 14.2.x does NOT use the async params pattern — that was introduced in Next.js 15. In Next.js 14, `params` is a plain synchronous object, not a Promise. The current code uses `Promise<{ id: string }>` and `await params`, which is wrong for Next.js 14.2.  

Now let me also check if there are other route files with the same incorrect pattern so I can fix all occurrences.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:44:07]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I understand the full picture:  

- `plugin-builder-service.ts` already derives the skill name from `skill.id` by splitting on `:` (line 249-250), so it doesn't need `name` on the type.  
- `agents-transfer-service.ts:441` uses `marketplaceSkill.name` — this is accessing a property that does NOT exist on the current `PluginSkillSelection` marketplace type, which means this is already a pre-existing bug.  

The finding correctly identifies that `name` is missing from the `onAddSkill` calls. Since `agents-transfer-service.ts` already tries to access `.name` on marketplace skill selections, the type needs to include `name`. I must add `name` to the `PluginSkillSelection` marketplace variant in the type, then pass it in both handlers.  

Let me now apply all fixes:  

**Fix 1**: Add `name` to the `marketplace` variant of `PluginSkillSelection` in `types/plugin-builder.ts`  
**Fix 2**: Add `name: skill.name` to the `onClick` handler in `SkillPicker.tsx`  
**Fix 3**: Add `name: skill.name` to the `onKeyDown` handler in `SkillPicker.tsx`    
**Fix 4**: Add `setMarketplaceSkills, setLoadingMarketplace` to the `useEffect` deps array  
**Fix 5**: The `aria-label` fix is functionally identical (same logic, just different ternary syntax) — it's a no-op change, but the finding says to apply it  

</div>

    20→export default function PluginComposer({  
    21→  name,

Now I have full context. `getSkillKey` is used inside `SkillGroup` at line 178. The import is at the top of the file (line 5). Since this is a single file, the import location (top of file) is the only valid place in TypeScript — you cannot do module imports inside a function. The report itself says "it's not a runtime error in TypeScript" and the proposed "fix" just moves the comment but keeps the import at module level. I'll skip this one as it's not a correctness bug.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:50:21]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the full picture. `PluginManifest` has these required fields: `name` (string), `version` (string), `output` (string), `plugin` (object), and `sources` (array). The bug is that the route only checks if `config.manifest` exists and is an object, but not if it conforms to the `PluginManifest` structure — an empty object `{}` would pass the check and cause `pushToGitHub` to fail downstream.  

The fix must validate the required fields of `PluginManifest`: `name`, `version`, `output`, `plugin`, and `sources`.  

</div>

**Old:**

  if (config.manifest === null || config.manifest === undefined || typeof config.manifest !== 'object') {

**New:**  
```
  // Explicit null check: typeof null === 'object', so guard against it
  if (config.manifest === null || config.manifest === undefined || typeof config.manifest !== 'object') {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Manifest is required' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }

  // Validate required PluginManifest fields so pushToGitHub always receives a complete manifest
  const manifest = config.manifest as Record<string, unknown>
  if (typeof manifest.name !== 'string' || !manifest.name) {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Manifest must contain a valid name' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
  if (typeof manifest.version !== 'string' || !manifest.version) {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Manifest must contain a valid version' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
  if (typeof manifest.output !== 'string' || !manifest.output) {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Manifest must contain a valid output path' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
  if (manifest.plugin === null || manifest.plugin === undefined || typeof manifest.plugin !== 'object') {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Manifest must contain a valid plugin metadata object' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
  if (!Array.isArray(manifest.sources)) {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Manifest must contain a sources array' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }

    41→    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {  
    42→      return NextResponse.json(  
    43→        { error: 'Invalid JSON in request body' },  
    44→        { status: 400 }  
    45→      )  
    46→    }  
    47→    return NextResponse.json(  
    48→      { error: 'Failed to scan repository due to an internal server error.' },  
    49→      { status: 500 }  
    50→    )  
    51→  }  
    52→}  
    53→

This means `activeOps` will be decremented twice for each successful build, leading to an incorrect count of active operations.    173→function evictStaleBuildResults(): void {

   571→async function runBuild(buildId: string, buildDir: string, manifest: PluginManifest): Promise<void> {  
   572→  const existing = buildResults.get(buildId)  
   573→  if (!existing) return  
   574→

   592→

   594→        await fs.access(path.join(outputPath, 'hooks', 'hooks.json'))  
   595→        stats.hooks = 1  
   596→      } catch {  
   597→        stats.hooks = 0  
   598→      }  
   599→    } catch {  
   600→      // Stats collection failed — non-critical  
   601→    }  
   602→  
   603→    // Atomic replacement: avoids torn reads from polling clients  
   604→    buildResults.set(buildId, {  
   605→      ...existing,  
   606→      status: 'complete',  
   607→      outputPath,  
   608→      logs: output.split('\n'),  
   609→      stats,

   612→    const message = error instanceof Error ? error.me

   475→export async function pushToGitHub(config: PluginPushConfig): Promise<ServiceResult<PluginPushResult>> {

   513→    )  
   514→  
   515→    // Stage and commit

This IS correct — when `runBuild` completes (success or the `.catch()` handles failure), `.finally()` decrements. But `runBuild` itself at lines 571-624 has NO `finally`. The report says BUG1: double decrement (remove the `.finally()` from `buildPlugin`) and BUG2: add `finally` to `runBuild`. These are two sides of the same fix. ## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:50:26]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have everything I need. Let me analyze the three bugs from the report:  

1. **BUG 1 (medium)**: `PluginSkillSelection` — the `marketplace` variant has a redundant `name` field alongside `plugin`. The `name` field for `marketplace` type is inconsistent with what `name` means in `core` and `repo` variants (skill name vs plugin name). The fix is to remove `name` from the `marketplace` variant.  

2. **BUG 2 (high)**: `PluginManifestSource` — the existing `id?: string` field comment says it's "required when multiple local sources share the same name", but it is not populated for marketplace skills where the `id` from `PluginSkillSelection` (type `marketplace`) needs to be stored. The fix is to add a `marketplaceId?: string` field, OR update the comment to clarify that the existing `id` field also serves for marketplace skill IDs. Since the `id` field already exists and adding `marketplaceId` would be a new field, the cleaner approach per the report is to update the existing `id` comment to reflect both uses.  

3. **BUG 3 (low)**: `PluginManifestMetadata` comment is misleading. Fix by clarifying it.  

Let me re-read BUG 2 carefully. The report says:  
- The `marketplace` variant has `id: string` that uniquely identifies the marketplace skill  
- `PluginManifestSource` has `id?: string` described as "required when multiple local sources share the same name"    
- When building from a `marketplace` skill, this `id` should be propagated to `PluginManifestSource`  
- The fix: add `marketplaceId?: string` field, OR update the comment on `id` to clarify it also stores marketplace skill IDs and ensure the build process populates it  

The existing `id` field already could serve this purpose — the issue is the comment doesn't reflect this. But the report also says adding `marketplaceId?: string` as a dedicated field would explicitly account for marketplace sources. Given that the `id` in `PluginSkillSelection` for `marketplace` type is the marketplace skill ID, and `PluginManifestSource.id` has a different semantic (disambiguating same-name local sources), adding a dedicated `marketplaceId?: string` is the proper fix for correctness.  

Now let me apply all three fixes.

    24→### BUG: Inconsistent Error Handling in `handle` method  
    25→**Severity**: medium  
    26→**Location**: `createHeadlessRouter().handle`  
    27→**Problem**: The `handle` method catches errors during route handling. If an error occurs and `res.headersSent` is true (meaning headers have already been sent, perhaps by a partial `sendServiceResult` or `sendJson` call before the error), the `sendJson` call for the 500 error will fail or cause a warning, as headers cannot be sent twice. This can lead to an incomplete or malformed response being sent to the client, or an unhandled exception in the server.

   270→// Utility helpers  
   271→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   272→  
   273→async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {  
   274→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   275→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   276→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   277→    req.on('end', () => {  
   278→      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')  
   279→      if (!body) return resolve({})  
   280→      try {  
   281→        resolve(JSON.parse(body))  
   282→      } catch (e) {  
   283→        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))  
   284→      }  
   285→    })  
   286→    req.on('error', reject)  
   287→  })  
   288→}  
   289→  
   290→async function readRawBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<Buffer> {  
   291→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   292→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   293→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   294→    req.on('end', () => resolve(Buffer.concat(chunks)))  
   295→    req.on('error', reject)  
   296→  })  
   297→}  
   298→  
   299→function sendJson(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, data: any, headers?: Record<string, string>) {  
   300→  const body = JSON.stringify(data)  
   301→  res.writeHead(statusCode, {  
   302→    'Content-Type': 'application/json',  
   303→    'Content-Length': Buffer.byteLength(body),  
   304→    ...headers,  
   305→  })  
   306→  res.end(body)  
   307→}  
   308→  
   309→function sendBinary(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, buffer: Buffer | Uint8Array, headers: Record<string, string>) {  
   310→  res.writeHead(statusCode, headers)  
   311→  res.end(buffer)  
   312→}

   316→  // result.data may also be present (e.g. partial results) but must not  
   317→  // suppress error reporting.  
   318→  if (result.error) {  
   319→    sendJson(res, result.st  

... [3260 more chars truncated]

  1283→function matchRoute(method: string, pathname: string): { handler: RouteHandler; params: Record<string, string> } | null {  
  1284→  for (const route of routes) {  
  1285→    if (route.method !== method) continue  
  1286→  
  1287→    const match = pathname.match(route.pattern)  
  1288→    if (!match) continue  
  1289→  
  1290→    const params: Record<string, string> = {}  
  1291→    route.paramNames.forEach((name, i) => {  
  1292→      params[name] = match[i + 1]  
  1293→    })  
  1294→  
  1295→    return { handler: route.handler, params }  
  1296→  }  
  1297→  return null  
  1298→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:51:07]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have all the information I need. Let me analyze the findings and apply each fix:  

**BUG 1** (medium): `createHeadlessRouter().handle` — missing `res.end()` when `headersSent` is true. Current code only handles `!res.headersSent`, needs to also end the response if headers were sent but not ended.  

**BUG 2** (low): `exportAgentZip` error path — current code at line 847 already uses `sendServiceResult` for errors (which is JSON-safe since on error `result.data` is not the binary blob). The report's suggested fix is actually already implemented at line 846-848. This is already correct — `sendServiceResult` is only called when `result.error` is true or `!result.data`, so no binary buffer leaks into JSON serialization. This BUG is already fixed in the current code.  

**BUG 3** (medium): `POST /api/agents/import` — `JSON.parse(optionsStr)` at line 578 can throw and fall through to generic catch. Fix: wrap in try/catch with specific error message.  

**BUG 4** (low): `sendJson` — `JSON.stringify` can throw on circular references. Fix: wrap in try/catch.  

**BUG 5** (low): Multiple `parseInt`/`parseFloat` calls without NaN checks. Fix: validate results.  

**BUG 6** (low): `query as any` for graph routes — `query` values are all strings but service expects `string | null` and `number`. Need to handle type conversion (especially `depth` which expects `number`).  

Let me now apply all fixes:  

</div>

      try {
        await matched.handler(req, res, matched.params, query)
      } catch (error) {

```

**New:**  
```
      try {
        await matched.handler(req, res, matched.params, query)
      } catch (error) {
        console.error(`[Headless] Error handling ${method} ${pathname}:`, error)
        if (!res.headersSent) {
          sendJson(res, 500, { error: 'Internal server error' })
        } else if (!res.writableEnded) {
          // Headers already sent (partial response started before the error); just
          // close the connection — we cannot send a new status code at this point.
          res.end()
        }
      }
```

**Old:**  
```
function sendJson(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, data: any, headers?: Record<string, string>) {
  const body = JSON.stringify(data)
  res.writeHead(statusCode, {
    'Content-Type': 'application/json',
    'Content-Length': Buffer.byteLength(body),
    ...headers,
  })
  res.end(body)
}
```

**New:**  
```
function sendJson(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, data: any, headers?: Record<string, string>) {
  let body: string
  try {
    body = JSON.stringify(data)
  } catch (e) {
    // Circular references or other non-serializable values — send a safe fallback.
    console.error('[Headless] Failed to serialize response data:', e)
    body = JSON.stringify({ error: 'Failed to serialize response data' })
    statusCode = 500
  }
  res.writeHead(statusCode, {
    'Content-Type': 'application/json',
    'Content-Length': Buffer.byteLength(body),
    ...headers,
  })
  res.end(body)
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-9a4b2a/services/headless-router.ts has been updated successfully.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:43:10]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I understand both issues clearly. Let me apply the fixes:  

1. **BUG 1**: The `catch` block returns a misleading 400 "Invalid request body" for all errors, including those thrown by `pushToGitHub` (which should be 500). Fix: distinguish `SyntaxError` (JSON parse failure → 400) from all other errors (→ 500).  

2. **BUG 2**: `request.json() as PluginPushConfig` type-asserts without runtime validation of the body itself being an object. Fix: validate the body is a non-null object before asserting the type, and also fix the `null` check for `manifest` (objects can be `null`).

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:43:22]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-9a4b2a/app/api/plugin-builder/push/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  try {
    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig

    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Manifest is required' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data)
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  let body: unknown
  try {
    // Parse JSON first — SyntaxError here means malformed request body
    body = await request.json()
  } catch (error) {

   273→async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {  
   274→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   275→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   276→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   277→    req.on('end', () => {  
   278→      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')  
   279→      if (!body) return resolve({})  
   280→      try {  
   281→        resolve(JSON.parse(body))  
   282→      } catch (e) {  
   283→        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))  
   284→      }  
   285→    })  
   286→    req.on('error', reject)  
   287→  })  
   288→}  
   289→  
   290→async function readRawBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<Buffer> {  
   291→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   292→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   293→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   294→    req.on('end', () => resolve(Buffer.concat(chunks)))  
   295→    req.on('error', reject)  
   296→  })  
   297→}  
   298→  
   299→function sendJson(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, data: any, headers?: Record<string, string>) {  
   300→  const body = JSON.stringify(data)  
   301→  res.writeHead(statusCode, {  
   302→    'Content-Type': 'application/json',  
   303→    'Content-Length': Buffer.byteLength(body),  
   304→    ...headers,  
   305→  })  
   306→  res.end(body)  
   307→}  
   308→  
   309→function sendBinary(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, buffer: Buffer | Uint8Array, headers: Record<string, string>) {  
   310→  res.writeHead(statusCode, headers)  
   311→  res.end(buffer)  
   312→}  
   313→  
   314→function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {  
   315→  if (result.error && !result.data) {  
   316→    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)  
   317→  } else {  
   318→    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)  
   319→  }  
   320→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:43:54]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Both `getAgentById` and `updateAgentById` are synchronous (no `async`), and `getSystemConfig` and `getOrganization` are also synchronous. So I must NOT add `await` to these — the bugs about missing `await` for those functions are not real for the current codebase. However, the findings about `sendServiceResult` condition and `parseMultipart` latin1 encoding, and inconsistent error handling patterns are valid.  

Let me carefully assess each bug:  

1. **BUG: `sendServiceResult` condition** - `result.error && !result.data` should be just `result.error` (medium severity)  
2. **BUG: `parseMultipart` latin1 encoding** - binary data corruption (high severity)   
3. **BUG: Missing `await` for `getSystemConfig` and `getOrganization`** - these are SYNC functions, NOT a bug  
4. **BUG: Inconsistent error handling for session activity** - low severity  
5. **BUG: Inconsistent error handling for agent export** - low severity    
6. **BUG: Inconsistent error handling for agent metadata** - low severity  
7. **BUG: Unhandled Promise Rejection in `handle`** - findings say "No direct code change strictly necessary"  
8. **BUG: `listSessions` error handling inconsistency** - low severity  
9. **BUG: `getAgentById` not awaited** - SYNC function, NOT a bug  
10. **BUG: `updateAgentById` not awaited** - SYNC function, NOT a bug  

For bugs 3, 9, 10: the functions are synchronous — adding `await` would be harmless (awaiting a non-promise returns the value), but the reported problem ("result being a Promise") doesn't exist. I'll skip these as the premise is false.  

For the consistency bugs (4, 5, 6, 8): The report suggests refactoring to use `sendServiceResult`. These are real inconsistencies. However, the existing handlers work correctly — they use `sendJson` which is the underlying function `sendServiceResult` calls. These are real issues I should fix.  

First let me fix bug #1 (`sendServiceResult` condition), then #2 (`parseMultipart`), then the consistency issues.  

</div>

```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  if (result.error && !result.data) {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)
  } else {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  // Presence of result.error is the sole indicator of an error response;
  // result.data may also be present (e.g. partial results) but must not
  // suppress error reporting.
  if (result.error) {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)
  } else {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)
  }
}
```

**Old:**  
```
/**
 * Minimal multipart form-data parser.
 * Handles the single use case: one file field + one text field for /api/agents/import.
 */
function parseMultipart(body: Buffer, contentType: string): { file: Buffer | null; options: string | null } {
  const boundaryMatch = contentType.match(/boundary=([^\s;]+)/)
  if (!boundaryMatch) return { file: null, options: null }

  const boundary = '--' + boundaryMatch[1]
  const bodyStr = body.toString('latin1')
  const parts = bodyStr.split(boundary).slice(1, -1) // Remove preamble and epilogue

  let file: Buffer | null = null
  let options: string | null = null

  for (const part of parts) {
    const headerEnd = part.indexOf('\r\n\r\n')
    if (headerEnd === -1) continue

    const headers = part.substring(0, headerEnd)
    const content = part.substring(headerEnd + 4).replace(/\r\n$/, '')

    if (headers.includes('name="file"')) {
      // Convert back to buffer from latin1 encoding
      file = Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')
    } else if (headers.includes('name="options"')) {
      options = content
    }
  }

  return { file, options }
}
```

**New:**  
```
/**
 * Minimal multipart form-data parser.
 * Handles the single use case: one file field + one text field for /api/agents/import.
 *
 * Operates entirely on raw Buffers so that binary file content is never corrupted
 * by a string encoding round-trip (the old latin1 approach mangled multi-byte data).
 * Only the MIME headers and plain-text fields are decoded as UTF-8.
 */
function parseMultipart(body: Buffer, contentType: string): { file: Buffer | null; options: string | null } {
  const boundaryMatch = contentType.match(/boundary=([^\s;]+)/)
  if (!boundaryMatch) return { file: null, options: null }

  const boundaryBuf = Buffer.from('--' + boundaryMatch[1])
  const crlfBuf = Buffer.from('\r\n')
  const doubleCrlfBuf = Buffer.from('\r\n\r\n')

  let fi

    // Return 400 only when the error is clearly a JSON parsing failure
    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Invalid request body: Malformed JSON' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    // All other unexpected errors are server-side; do not mislead the client
    return NextResponse.json(

      { status: 500 }
    )
  }

   556→/**  
   557→ * Run build-plugin.sh in the build directory and capture output.  
   558→ * Uses atomic replacement of the map entry to avoid torn reads.  
   559→ */  
   560→async function runBuild(buildId: string, buildDir: string, manifest: PluginManifest): Promise<void> {  
   561→  const existing = buildResults.get(buildId)  
   562→  if (!existing) return  
   563→  
   564→  try {  
   565→    const output = await execPromise(  
   566→      path.join(buildDir, 'build-plugin.sh'),  
   567→      ['--clean'],  
   568→      { cwd: buildDir, timeout: 120000 }  
   569→    )  
   570→  
   571→    // Parse output for stats  
   572→    const outputPath = path.join(buildDir, manifest.output)  
   573→    const stats = { skills: 0, scripts: 0, hooks: 0 }  
   574→  
   575→    try {  
   576→      const skillEntries = await fs.readdir(path.join(outputPath, 'skills')).catch(() => [] as string[])  
   577→      stats.skills = skillEntries.length  
   578→  
   579→      const scriptEntries = await fs.readdir(path.join(outputPath, 'scripts')).catch(() => [] as string[])  
   580→      stats.scripts = scriptEntries.length  
   581→  
   582→      try {  
   583→        await fs.access(path.join(outputPath, 'hooks', 'hooks.json'))  
   584→        stats.hooks = 1  
   585→      } catch {  
   586→        stats.hooks = 0  
   587→      }  
   588→    } catch {  
   589→      // Stats collection failed — non-critical  
   590→    }  
   591→  
   592→    // Atomic replacement: avoids torn reads from polling clients  
   593→    buildResults.set(buildId, {  
   594→      ...existing,  
   595→      status: 'complete',  
   596→      outputPath,  
   597→      logs: output.split('\n'),  
   598→      stats,  
   599→    })  
   600→  } catch (error: unknown) {  
   601→    const message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)  
   602→    const stderr = (error as any)?.stderr  
   603→    const logs = [message]  
   604→    if (stderr) logs.push(...String(stderr).split('\n'))  
   605→  
   606→    // Atomic replacement  
   607→    buildResults.set  

... [2737 more chars truncated]

   684→/**

   687→function sanitizeSourceName(url: string): string {  
   688→  return url  
   689→    .replace(/^https?:\/\//, '')

   697→/**  
   698→ * Promisified execFile with stdout capture.  
   699→ */  
   700→function execPromise(  
   701→  command: string,  
   702→  args: string[],  
   703→  options: { cwd?: string; timeout?: number } = {}  
   704→): Promise<string> {  
   705→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   706→    execFile(command, args, {  
   707→      cwd: options.cwd,  
   708→      timeout: options.timeout || 60000,  
   709→      maxBuffer: 2 * 1024 * 1024, // 2MB (reduced from 10MB)  
   710→    }, (error, stdout, stderr) => {  
   711→      if (error) {  
   712→        const err = error as any  
   713→        err.stderr = stderr  
   714→        reject(err)  
   715→      } else {  
   716→        resolve(stdout)  
   717→      }  
   718→    })  
   719→  })  
   720→}  
   721→  
   722→/**  
   723→ * Recursively copy a directory, skipping symlinks.  
   724→ */  
   725→async function copyDir(src: string, dest: string): Promise<void> {  
   726→  await fs.mkdir(dest, { recursive: true })  
   727→  const entries = await fs.readdir(src, { withFileTypes: true })  
   728→  for (const entry of entries) {  
   729→    // Skip symlinks to prevent copying files outside the source tree  
   730→    if (entry.isSymbolicLink()) continue  
   731→  
   732→    const srcPath = path.join(src, entry.name)  
   733→    const destPath = path.join(dest, entry.name)  
   734→    if (entry.isDirectory()) {  
   735→      await copyDir(srcPath, destPath)  
   736→    } else {  
   737→      await fs.copyFile(srcPath, destPath)  
   738→

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:43:49]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I'll apply all fixes. Starting with the fixes that can be done in parallel:  

**Fix 1**: `activeOps` decrement — replace `Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)` with `activeOps--` everywhere (3 locations).  

**Fix 2**: `execPromise` — ensure `stderr` is always properly attached (already does this, but the report says to make it cleaner — looking at the code, `execPromise` already does `err.stderr = stderr` before `reject(err)`, so this is already correct. **Fix 3**: `evictStaleBuildResults` — log errors from `fs.rm`.  

**Fix 4**: `scanRepo` catch — include `stderr` in error message.

    const message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)

   173→function evictStaleBuildResults(): void {  
   174→  const now = Date.now()  
   175→  for (const [id, result] of buildResults) {  
   176→    const age = now - new Date(result.createdAt).getTime()  
   177→    if (age > BUILD_TTL_MS) {  
   178→      buildResults.delete(id)  
   179→      // Best-effort cleanup of build directory  
   180→      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)  
   181→      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(err => {  
   182→        console.error(`Failed to remove build directory ${id}:`, err)  
   183→      })  
   184→    }  
   185→  }  
   186→  
   187→  // If still over limit, evict oldest  
   188→  if (buildResults.size > MAX_BUILD_RESULTS) {  
   189→    const entries = [...buildResults.entries()]  
   190→      .sort((a, b) => new Date(a[1].createdAt).getTime() - new Date(b[1].createdAt).getTime())  
   191→    const toRemove = entries.slice(0, entries.length - MAX_BUILD_RESULTS)  
   192→    for (const [id] of toRemove) {  
   193→      buildResults.delete(id)  
   194→      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)  
   195→      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(err => {  
   196→        console.error(`Failed to remove build directory ${id} during eviction:`, err)  
   197→      })  
   198→    }  
   199→  }  
   200→}

   397→/**  
   398→ * Get the status of a running or completed build.

   400→export async function getBuildStatus(buildId: string): Promise<ServiceResult<PluginBuildResult>> {

   405→  if (!result) {

   472→/**  
   473→ * Push a generated manifest to the user's fork on GitHub.  
   474→ */  
   475→export async function pushToGitHub(config: PluginPushConfig): Promise<ServiceResult<PluginPushResult>> {  
   476→  // Validate fork URL  
   477→  if (!config.forkUrl || typeof config.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
   478→    return { error: 'Fork URL is required', status: 400 }  
   479→  }  
   480→  const urlErr = validateGitUrl(config.forkUrl)  
   481→  if (urlErr) return { error: urlErr, status: 400 }  
   482→

Now I can see both the issue and the exact code. The bug is on lines 45 and 51 — the regex allows plugin names ending with `-` or `_`. The fix requires the regex to also enforce the name ends with an alphanumeric character. However, the fix must also handle single-character names (e.g., `"a"`) which would fail `[a-zA-Z0-9_-]*[a-zA-Z0-9]$` if the minimum is 1 char. Let me check: `^[a-zA-Z0-9][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*[a-zA-Z0-9]$` requires at least 2 characters. A single-character name like `"a"` would be rejected, which is correct behaviour. I'll apply both fixes now.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:50:24]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the full picture. I need to apply two fixes:  

**BUG 1 (medium):** `handleAddSkill` uses the live `url`/`ref` state which may have changed since the scan. Fix: add `lastScannedUrl`/`lastScannedRef` state, set them after a successful scan, use them in `handleAddSkill` and for the `key` computation in JSX.  

**BUG 2 (low):** The `ref` `onChange` handler forces `'main'` on empty input, while `handleScan` doesn't have that same default. Fix: remove `|| 'main'` from `onChange`, add `ref.trim() || 'main'` in `handleScan`.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:43:29]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The `description` field in `PluginBuildConfig` is typed as `description?: string` (optional, meaning `string | undefined`). So both `string` and `undefined` are valid. However, the bug is about inconsistency: the state is initialized as `''` (empty string), but the `buildConfig` converts it to `undefined` when it's an empty string. The finding asks to remove the `|| undefined` conversion so `description` stays consistent as an empty string when not provided.  

Let me also check how the service uses `description` to make sure removing the `|| undefined` doesn't break downstream behavior.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:43:34]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The service directly uses `config.description` and passes it into the manifest where `description?: string`. Both `''` and `undefined` are valid there. However, the bug report correctly identifies that the conversion `description || undefined` introduces inconsistency — the state starts as `''` but `buildConfig` silently converts it to `undefined`. The fix is to pass `description` directly without the `|| undefined` coercion.  

Now I'll apply the fix.  

</div>
